    k &\mapsto  \rho^{\mathcal H}_h \rho^{{\mathcal G}^1}_k \rho^{\mathcal H}_{h^{-1}}\\
    k &\mapsto  \rho^{{\mathcal G}^1}_{hkh^{-1}}.
  \end{align*}
  The readily computed derivatives are:
  \begin{align*}
    X &\mapsto \rho^{\mathcal H}_h \adjoint^\tau_X \rho^{\mathcal H}_{h^{-1}}(\,\cdot\,)
        = \rho^{\mathcal H}_h \tau(X, \rho^{\mathcal H}_{h^{-1}}(\,\cdot\,))\\
    \text{and}\quad X &\mapsto \adjoint^\tau_{\Adjoint_hX}(\,\cdot\,)=\tau(\Adjoint_hX, \,\cdot\,) =
                        \tau(\rho^{\mathcal H}_h X, \,\cdot\,),\quad\text{by \eqref{pony4}}.
  \end{align*}
  Equality of these derivatives follows from the $\rho^{\mathcal H}$-invariance of $\tau $.

  Proof of the remaining claims of the proposition is elementary and omitted.
\end{proof}

% Some of our notions of compatibility are summarized in Table 1.
% \begin{table}[]
% \centering
%   \begin{tabular}{@{}|c|c|c|c|@{}}
%   \toprule
%   compatibility of $\downarrow$ with $\rightarrow$ & $\tau$   & $\nabla$                        &  $\epsilon$\\ \midrule
%   filtration & $\tau(A^j, A^k) \subset A^{j+k}$ &  $A^j$ is $\bar\nabla$-invariant $\forall j$ & -   \\
%   $\tau$     &                                 &  $\tau $ is $\bar\nabla $-invariant  & $\graded_0(e)$ grades $\graded_T(A)$ \\
%   $\nabla $  &                                 &                                      &  $\epsilon$ is $\bar\nabla $-invariant \\  \bottomrule
% \end{tabular}
% \vspace{0.75\baselineskip}
% \caption{Summary of compatibility conditions for structures on a filtered Lie algebroid
%   $A$. Here $\tau $ model data, $T=\graded_0(\tau)$, $\nabla $ is an infinitesimal Cartan
%   connection, and $\epsilon$ a Weyl gauge.}
% \end{table}

\subsection{Gradings associated with model data}\label{model_data_gradings}

Let us say that model data $\tau$ is {\df compatible} with a Weyl gauge
$\epsilon \in \Gamma(A^0)$ if $E = \graded_0(\epsilon)$ is a fibre-wise grading element of
$\graded^T(A)$, $T=\graded_0(\tau)$, and not just of $\graded(A^0)=\graded^T(A^0)$.

Let $A$ be a filtered Lie algebroid admitting a Weyl gauge $\epsilon$. Then, according to
Theorem \ref{weyl}, we have an associated grading $A^0=\oplus_{i\ge 0}{\mathfrak a}_i$
that is invariant under the action of the isotropy subalgebroid $B \subset A$ of
$\epsilon$. If $\epsilon$ is compatible with model data $\tau$, that is itself compatible
with the filtration of $A$, then this grading extends to a grading
$A = \oplus_i {\mathfrak a}_i $, where $X \in {\mathfrak a}_j$ if and only if
$\tau(\epsilon, X) = jX$. This defines a splitting isomorphism
$\Phi_\epsilon \colon \graded^T(A) \rightarrow A$.

\begin{proposition} {\em \bfseries Infinitesimal case.} In the scenario above, let $\nabla $ be any
  infinitesimal Cartan connection weakly compatible with $\tau $. Then:
  \begin{conditions}
  \item The grading $A = \oplus_i {\mathfrak a}_i$ is invariant under the representation
    $\bar\nabla $ of $B$ on $A$.    \label{u4}
  \item For any $X \in \Gamma({\mathfrak a}_k)$, $k\ge 0$, and
    $Y \in \Gamma({\mathfrak a}_j)$, $j \in {\mathbb Z} $, one has
    $\bar\nabla_XY \in \Gamma({\mathfrak a}_j \oplus {\mathfrak a}_{j+k})$.\label{u3}
%  \item $\nabla $ is compatible with the filtration of $A$. \label{u7}
  \end{conditions}
  {\em\bfseries Global case.} If ${\mathcal G} $ is a weakly firm, filtered Lie groupoid with Lie
  algebroid $A$, $\epsilon$ is a Weyl gauge for ${\mathcal G} $ compatible with the model data
  $\tau $, and $D$ is a Cartan connection on ${\mathcal G} $ compatible with $\tau $,
  then:
  \begin{conditions}
  \item The grading $A=\oplus_i {\mathfrak a}_i$ associated with $\epsilon$ is invariant under
    the representation $\bar D $ of the isotropy subgroupoid
    ${\mathcal H}\subset {\mathcal G} $ of $\epsilon$.\label{uu4}
%  \item $D$ is compatible with the filtration of $A$.\label{uu7}
  \end{conditions}
\end{proposition}

The reader is warned that $B$ does not generally align itself with the complement
$\oplus_{i\le 0}{\mathfrak a}_i$ of $A^1=\oplus_{i\ge 1}{\mathfrak a}_i$ in $A$ defined by
the grading.  We may only conclude that $B$ is the graph of some linear function
$\oplus_{j\le 0} {\mathfrak a}_i \rightarrow A^1$ that vanishes on ${\mathfrak a}_0$,
which is necessarily contained in $B$.

\begin{corollary}
  If a (weakly firm) filtered Lie algebroid (resp., Lie groupoid) admits a Weyl gauge
  compatible with some model data $\tau $, then any Cartan connection weakly compatible with
  $\tau $ is compatible with the filtration.
\end{corollary}

\begin{proof}[Proof of corollary]
  If $\nabla $ is the Cartan connection in the Lie algebroid case, then
  $\bar\nabla$-invariance of the filtration of $A$ follows from \eqref{u4} and \eqref{u3},
  and the semi-direct product structure of $A$ (Theorem \eqrefs{weyl}{pq2}).

  For the Lie groupoid case and a global Cartan connection $D$, we know the filtration is
  $\bar\nabla $-invariant, where $\nabla $ is the infinitesimalization of $D$, from the
  Lie algebroid case just proven. In particular, continuing in the notation of the
  proposition, the restriction of $\bar\nabla $ to a representation of $A^1$ on $A$ is
  filtration-preserving. Therefore, the restriction of $\bar D$ to a representation of
  ${\mathcal G}^1$ is filtration-preserving, because ${\mathcal G}^1$ is source-connected.
  Full ${\bar D}$-invariance of the filtration follows from this fact, \eqref{uu4}, and
  the semi-direct product structure of $\mathcal G$ (Theorem \eqrefs{weyl2}{pr2}).
\end{proof}
%
\begin{proof}[Proof of proposition]
  Our proofs of \eqref{u4} and \eqref{u3} are variations on an argument appearing in the
  proof of Theorem \ref{weyl}.  Indeed, suppose that $Y \in \Gamma({\mathfrak a}_j)$ for
  some $j$ and let $X \in \Gamma(B)$ be arbitrary. Then, applying $\bar\nabla_X$ to both
  sides of the identity $\tau(\epsilon, Y) = jY$, and appealing to the
  $\bar\nabla$-invariance of $\tau$ (weak compatability), we have
\begin{equation*}
    \tau(\bar\nabla_{X}\epsilon, Y) + \tau(\epsilon, \bar\nabla_XY) = j \bar\nabla_XY.
\end{equation*}
But $\bar\nabla_{X} \epsilon = [X, \epsilon]$, because $\epsilon$ is in the anchor kernel, while $[X, \epsilon] = 0 $,
because $X \in \Gamma(B)$. We conclude that $\bar\nabla_XY \in \Gamma({\mathfrak
  a}_j)$. This proves \eqref{u4}.

Turning to \eqref{u3}, write $\bar\nabla_XY=\sum_iW_i$ for
  some $W_i \in \Gamma({\mathfrak a}_i)$, which implies
\begin{equation*}
    \tau(\epsilon, \bar\nabla_XY) = \sum_iiW_i.
\end{equation*}
On the other hand, $\tau(\epsilon, Y) = jY$, which, after applying $\bar\nabla_X$ to both
sides, and appealing to the $\bar\nabla$-invariance of $\tau $, becomes
\begin{equation*}
  \tau(\bar\nabla_X \epsilon, Y) + \tau(\epsilon, \bar\nabla_XY) = j\sum_iW_i.
\end{equation*}
As $X$ and $\epsilon$ are sections of $A^0$, we have
$\bar\nabla_X E = [X, \epsilon] = \tau(X, \epsilon) = -kX$. From this and the two preceding equations we
deduce
\begin{equation*}
   \sum_i(i-j)W_i + k \tau(Y, X) =0.
\end{equation*}
Since $A = \oplus_i {\mathfrak a}_i$ is a grading with respect to $\tau$, the last term on
the left-hand side is a section of $\Gamma({\mathfrak a}_{j+k})$. Projecting onto each
component ${\mathfrak a}_i$ of the grading $A = \oplus_i {\mathfrak a}_i$, we obtain
$W_i = 0$ for all $i$, with the possible exceptions $i=j, j+k$, which shows
$\bar\nabla_XY \in \Gamma({\mathfrak a}_j \oplus {\mathfrak a}_{j+k})$.

The proof of \eqref{uu4} is similar to that of \eqref{u4} above, following from the
$\bar D$-invariance of $\tau $, the definition of the spaces ${\mathfrak a}_j$, and the
fact that ${\mathcal H} $ fixes $\epsilon$.
\end{proof}

% \begin{corollary}
%   Every gauge transformation $\varphi \colon A \rightarrow A$ induces the identity in
%   homology $H_n(A^1, A) \rightarrow H_n(A^1, A)$.
% \end{corollary}

\refreshpage
\section{Filtered Cartan geometries}\label{filtered_cartan}
Suppose ${\mathcal G} $ is a firmly filtered Lie groupoid, with Lie algebroid $A$,
supporting a Cartan connection $D$ compatible with the filtration, and model data $\tau $
compatible with the filtration. Then we call $({\mathcal G}, D, \tau)$ a {\df filtered
  Cartan geometry} if:
\begin{conditions}
   \item $\tau $ is compatible with $D$ (in the sense of \ref{preview}).
   \item ${\mathcal G}$ admits a Weyl gauge compatible with $\tau $.\label{fc2}
\end{conditions}
Because we assume ${\mathcal G} $ is firmly filtered, \eqref{fc2} just means
${\mathcal G}$ admits an $\Adjoint$-invariant, fibre-wise grading section of
$\graded^T(A)$, where $T:=\graded_0(\tau)$ (Corollary \ref{weyl2}). There is no
requirement here that $\tau $ be reductive or semisimple, and such notions will play no
role in the current section. However, Proposition \ref{all}, stated later, shows that every
parabolic geometry is a filtered Cartan geometry.

If we only have a firmly filtered Lie algebroid $A$, and an infinitesimal Cartan
connection $\nabla$, compatible with the filtration and compatible with $\tau $,
and if $A$ admits a $\tau$-compatible Weyl gauge, then $(A, \nabla, \tau)$ is an {\df
  infinitesimal filtered Cartan geometry}.

In this section, we provide a general, explicit, description of {\em transitive}, filtered
Cartan geometries, by exploiting theorems on semi-direct product structure established in
Section \ref{semi-direct}. In this description, we specify the additional data needed to
recover a transitive Cartan geometry from its (abstract) Levi reduction. While we are
mainly interested in the special parabolic case, the extra abstraction introduced here
emphasizes Weyl gauges as the essential actor in the resulting characterization.

\subsection{Abstract Levi structures: the infinitesimal case}\label{inflevi}
The reduction procedure described for parabolic geometries in \ref{reduction_} generalizes
to transitive filtered Cartan geometries. We begin with the infinitesimal case.

Let $(A, \nabla, \tau)$ be a transitive infinitesimal filtered Cartan geometry. Since $A$
is firmly filtered, the canonical representation $\adjoint$ of $A$ on $A^0$, in which
$A^1$ is acting trivially, descends to a representation $\adjoint$ of $B:=A/A^1$ on
$\graded(A^0)$. This canonical representation is extended by a representation of $B$ on
$\graded(A)$, induced by the representation $\bar\nabla $ of $A$ on itself, and we denote
this by $R^\nabla$. If we write ${\mathfrak a}_j:=\graded(A)_j$ for $j>0$, then using the
transitivity we can write
\begin{conditions}
  \item[{\bfseries C0.}]
  \quad $\graded(A) \cong \graded(TM)\oplus B^0 \oplus (\oplus_{j>0}{\mathfrak a}_j)$.
\end{conditions}
In addition to the grading-preserving representation $R^\nabla$ on the above, we have the
Lie algebra bundle bracket $T := \graded_0(\tau)$ which, on account of the compatibility
Axiom c2, shows that
\begin{equation}
  \label{form_}
  T(C, V) = R^\nabla_C V,\quad
  T(C, Z) = R^\nabla_C Z,\quad
  T(C, C') = [C,C'],
\end{equation}
whenever $C,C'\in\Gamma(B^0)$, $V\in \Gamma(\graded(TM))$,
$Z \in \Gamma(\oplus_{j>0} {\mathfrak a}_j)$. The last equation holds because $\tau$
extends the canonical bracket on $A^0$. Note $R^\nabla Z$ does not actually depend on
$\nabla $, because it is determined by the canonical representation of $A$ on $A^1$.

Motivated by the above, an {\df abstract infinitesimal Levi structure} will be a 4-tuple
$(B, \oplus_{j>0} {\mathfrak a}_j, R, T)$, where:
\begin{conditions}
  \item $B$ is a transitive, filtered Lie algebroid over $M$ with $B \le 0$ and with $B^0$
    as its anchor kernel.
  \item $\oplus_{j>0}{\mathfrak a}_j$ is a graded vector bundle over $M$, with
    ${\mathfrak a}_j=0$ for all sufficiently large $j$.
  \item $R$ is a a grading-preserving representation of $B$ on C0 that extends
    the canonical action of $B$ on $B^0$
  \item\label{chh0} $T$ is an $R$-invariant Lie algebra bundle structure on C0
    compatible with the obvious grading and satisfying
    \begin{equation*}
      T(C, V) = R_C V,\quad
      T(C, Z) = R_C Z,\quad
      T(C, C') = [C,C'],
    \end{equation*}
    whenever $C,C'\in\Gamma(B^0)$, $V\in \Gamma(\graded(TM))$,
    $Z \in \Gamma(\oplus_{j>0} {\mathfrak a}_j)$.
  \item\label{six} As a graded Lie algebra bundle, C0 admits an $R$-invariant grading section,
    necessarily of the form $(0, E, 0)$, for some $E \in \Gamma(B^0)$, where $E$ is required to
    commute with arbitrary sections of $B$.
\end{conditions}
\noindent Note that it is not required that $T$ restrict to the canonical Lie algebra
bundle structure on $\graded(TM)$. If this restriction is the {\em negative} of the
canonical one, then the Levi structure is {\df regular}.

According to the immediately preceding observations, associated with every transitive
infinitesimal filtered Cartan geometry is an infinitesimal Levi structure, called its {\df
  Levi reduction}, regular if the filtered Cartan geometry is regular.

\subsection{Abstract Levi structures: the global case}\label{abstract_levi}%
\mbox{}\newline
\noindent%
An {\df abstract Levi structure} is a 4-tuple
$({\mathcal H}, \oplus_{j>0}{\mathfrak a}_j, R, T)$ where:
\begin{conditions}
  \item ${\mathcal H} $ is a transitive, filtered Lie groupoid over $M$ with Lie algebroid
    $B$, whose anchor kernel is $B^0$, and with $B \le 0$.
  \item $\oplus_{j>0}{\mathfrak a}_j$ is a graded vector bundle over $M$, with
    ${\mathfrak a}_j=0$ for all sufficiently large $j$.
  \item $R$ is a grading-preserving representation of ${\mathcal H}$ on
    C0 that extends the canonical action of ${\mathcal H}$ on $B^0$.
   \item\label{chh00} $T$ an $R$-invariant Lie algebra bundle structure on
    C0 compatible with the grading, and such that
    \begin{equation*}
      T(C, V) = dR_C V,\quad
      T(C, Z) = dR_C Z,\quad
      T(C, C') = [C,C'],
    \end{equation*}
    for all $C,C'\in\Gamma(B^0)$, $V\in \Gamma(\graded(TM))$,
    $Z \in \Gamma(\oplus_{j>0} {\mathfrak a}_j)$.
  \item\label{five} As a graded Lie algebra bundle, C0 admits an $R$-invariant grading
    section, necessarily of the form $(0, E, 0)$, for some $E \in \Gamma(B^0)$, where $E$
    is required to be ${\mathcal H} $-invariant.
\end{conditions}
Here $dR$ is the infinitesimalization of the representation $R$. The structure is {\df
  regular} if its infinitesimalization $(B,\oplus_{j>0}{\mathfrak a}_j, dR, T)$ is
regular.  %

In analogy with our observations in \ref{inflevi}, we can associate with each transitive
filtered Cartan geometry $({\mathcal G}, D, \tau)$ an abstract Levi structure
$({\mathcal G}/{\mathcal G}^1, \graded(A^1), R^D, \graded_0(\tau))$ that we call its {\df
  Levi reduction}. It is regular if $({\mathcal G}, D, \tau)$ is. Here $R^D$ is the
representation of ${\mathcal G}/{\mathcal G}^1$ induced by the representation $\bar D$ of
${\mathcal G} $ on the Lie algebroid $A$ of ${\mathcal G} $.

\subsection{Morphisms}\label{morphisms}
A {\df morphism} of filtered Lie algebroids $q \colon A \rightarrow \tilde A$ is a Lie
algebroid morphism respecting the filtrations: $q(A^j) \subset \tilde A^j$. A {\df
  morphism} of filtered Lie groupoids
$Q \colon {\mathcal G} \rightarrow \tilde {\mathcal G} $ is a Lie groupoid morphism whose
infinitesimalization $q=dQ \colon A \rightarrow \tilde A$ is a morphism of firmly filtered
Lie algebroids. (Infinitesimal) Weyl gauge transformations are examples of automorphisms
of a filtered Lie groupoid (resp., Lie algebroid). We obtain the category of {\em firmly}
filtered Lie algebroids or Lie groupoids by simply restricting the class of morphisms to
those whose source and target are firmly filtered objects.

For simplicity, and as it will suffice for current purposes, we only define morphisms for
filtered Cartan geometries that are isomorphisms. A {\df morphism} of infinitesimal filtered
Cartan geometries
$$(A, \tau, \nabla) \rightarrow (\tilde A, \tilde \tau, \tilde \nabla)$$ is an isomorphism of
underlying filtered Lie algebroids such that $\tau$ and $\nabla $ push forward to
$\tilde \tau $ and $\tilde \nabla $; since $q$ is an isomorphism, pushing forward makes
sense.  A {\df morphism} of global filtered Cartan geometries $({\mathcal G}, \tau, D)$
and $(\tilde {\mathcal G}, \tilde \tau, \tilde D)$ is an isomorphism of underlying
filtered Lie groupoids that pushes $\tau $ and $D $ to $\tilde \tau$
and $\tilde D $.

A morphism of abstract infinitesimal Levi structures
$$(B, \oplus_{j>0} {\mathfrak a}_j, R, T) \rightarrow
(\tilde B, \oplus_{j>0} \tilde{\mathfrak a}_j, \tilde R, \tilde T)$$
consists of a pair $(q, \omega)$, where $q \colon B \rightarrow \tilde B$ is morphism of
filtered Lie algebroids, covering some smooth map $f \colon M \rightarrow \tilde M$, and
$\omega \colon \oplus_{j>0}{\mathfrak a}_j \rightarrow \oplus_{j>0}\tilde{\mathfrak a}_j$
a morphism of graded vector bundles, such that induced morphisms of graded vector bundles
\begin{gather*}
  (q, \omega)_* \colon \graded(TM)\oplus B^0 \oplus (\oplus_{j>0}{\mathfrak a}_j)
     \rightarrow \graded(TM)\oplus \tilde B^0 \oplus (\oplus_{j>0}\tilde{\mathfrak a}_j)\\
  (V, C, Z) \mapsto (\graded_0(Tf)(V), qC, \omega Z)
\end{gather*}
is: (i) a morphism of Lie algebra bundles, with respect to the brackets $T$ and
$\tilde T$; and (ii) an intertwining of the representations $R$ and $\tilde R$. Here
$Tf \colon TM \rightarrow TM$ is the tangent map of $f$, which will necessarily be
filtration-preserving because $\# \circ q = Tf \circ \#$. A morphism of abstract Levi
structures $({\mathcal H}, \oplus_{j>0}{\mathfrak a}_j, R, T)$ and
$(\tilde {\mathcal H}, \oplus_{j>0}\tilde{\mathfrak a}_j, \tilde R, \tilde T)$ is a pair
$(Q, \omega)$, where $Q \colon {\mathcal H} \rightarrow \tilde {\mathcal H} $ is morphism
of filtered Lie groupoids and
$\omega \colon \oplus_{j>0}{\mathfrak a}_j \rightarrow \oplus_{j>0}\tilde{\mathfrak a}_j$
a morphism of graded vector bundles, such that: (i) $(dQ, \omega)$ is a morphism of the
corresponding abstract infinitesimal Levi structures; and (ii) $(dQ, \omega)_*$
intertwines the (global) representations $R$ and $\tilde R$.

As it turns out, for the applications we have in mind, only morphisms of infinitesimal or
global Levi structures covering the identity on $M$ will be relevant, in which case $f$
above is just the identity.

\subsection{Consequences of the semi-direct product structure}\label{consequences}%
Beginning our analysis with the infinitesimal case, suppose $(A, \nabla, \tau)$ is a
transitive infinitesimal filtered Cartan geometry such that $A^0$ is the anchor kernel, and let
$\epsilon $ be a $\tau$-compatible gauge. According to Theorem \ref{weyl}, we may suppose,
without loss of generality, that $A$ is the semi-direct product of a transitive, filtered
Lie algebroid $B$, with $|B| \le 0$ and anchor $B^0$, with a filtered Lie algebra bundle
$\oplus_{j>0}{\mathfrak a}_j$, on which $B $ is acting, an action that preserves the
grading. Moreover, if we denote the action of $B$ on $\oplus_{j>0}{\mathfrak a}_j$ by $R$,
so that $A = B \oplus_R(\oplus_{j>0}{\mathfrak a}_j)$, then we know there exists a section
$E$ of $B^0$ such that:
\begin{gather*}
  [E, X]=0\quad \text{for all $X \in \Gamma(B)$}\\
  R_EY = jY\quad\text{for all $Y \in \Gamma({\mathfrak a}_j)$, $j>0$}.\\
  \epsilon = (E, 0) \in \Gamma(A).
\end{gather*}
The Weyl gauge determines a grading $A = \oplus_i {\mathfrak a}'_i$, where
${\mathfrak a}'_i$ is the kernel of
$X \mapsto \tau(E,X) - iX \colon A^i \rightarrow A^{i+1}$.

In general, ${\mathfrak a}'_k \subset B \oplus 0$ does not hold for $k <0$. However,
noting that the filtration of $A=B\oplus_R (\oplus_{j>0}{\mathfrak a}_j)$ is defined by
$A^i = B^i \oplus_R(\oplus_{j\ge\max\{1,i\}}{\mathfrak a}_j)$, it is not hard to see,
from the identities above, that ${\mathfrak a}'_0=B^0 \oplus 0$ and
${\mathfrak a}'_j=0\oplus{\mathfrak a}_j$ for $j> 0$.  From this we may deduce that the
splitting isomorphism $\Phi\colon \graded(A) \rightarrow A$ induced by the grading
$A = \oplus_i {\mathfrak a}'_i$ has the form
\begin{gather*}
    \Phi \colon \graded(TM) \oplus B^0 \oplus (\oplus_{j>0} {\mathfrak a}_j)
    \rightarrow B\oplus_R(\oplus_{j>0}{\mathfrak a}_j)\\
    (V, C, Z) \mapsto (C + \tilde \sigma (V), Z - \mathsf{P}(V)),
\end{gather*}
for some $\mathsf{P} \subset \Gamma(\graded(T^*\!M)\otimes(\oplus_{j>0}{\mathfrak a}_j))$,
and some vector bundle map $\tilde \sigma \colon \graded(TM) \rightarrow B$ satisfying
\begin{equation*}
  \tilde \sigma(\graded(TM)_k) \subset B^k\enspace\text{and}\enspace
    \graded_k(\# \tilde \sigma (V)) = V \quad\text{for all $V \in \graded(TM)_k$, $k < 0$}.
\end{equation*}
Here $\# \colon B \rightarrow TM$ denotes the anchor. This is just linear algebra and an
unpacking of the implicit identification
${\mathfrak a}_k\cong\graded(A)_k \cong \graded(TM)_k$ for $k < 0$.

The composite $\sigma=\#\circ\tilde\sigma $ satisfies
\begin{equation*}
  \sigma(\graded(TM)_k) \subset T^kM\enspace\text{and}\enspace
    \graded_k(\sigma (V)) = V \quad\text{for all $V \in \graded(TM)_k$, $k < 0$}.
\end{equation*}
We call such $\sigma \colon \graded(TM) \rightarrow TM $, which is necessarily an
isomorphism, a {\df splitting} of the filtered manifold $M$. The composite
$s = \tilde \sigma \circ \sigma^{-1} \colon TM \rightarrow B$ is a right-inverse for the
anchor $\# \colon B \rightarrow TM$, which we will call a {\df splitting of the anchor of $B$}. We
may now rewrite our formula for $\Phi $ as
\begin{conditions}\item[{\bfseries S1.}]
  \quad $\Phi(V, C, Z) = (C + s(\sigma(V)), Z - \mathsf{P}(V))$.
\end{conditions}
By construction, the model data $\tau $ is the push-forward of $T:=\graded_0(\tau)$ under
$\Phi $:
\begin{conditions}\item[{\bfseries S2.}]
  \quad $\tau(\Phi(\xi_1), \Phi(\xi_2)) = \Phi(T(\xi_1, \xi_2))$,
\end{conditions}
for $\xi_1,\,\xi_2 \in \graded(TM)\oplus B \oplus_R(\oplus_{j>0}{\mathfrak a}_j)$, and
$(0, E, 0)$ is a fibre-wise grading section of
$\graded(TM) \oplus B^0 \oplus (\oplus_j {\mathfrak a}_j)$, for the Lie bracket $T$.  To
complete our analysis, we derive a formula for the self-representation $\bar\nabla $ of
$A$, which characterizes the connection $\nabla$, because $A$ is transitive (Proposition
\ref{hsd}).  Since Proposition \ref{model_data_gradings} applies, the grading
$A=\oplus_i {\mathfrak a}'_i$ (there denoted $\oplus_i {\mathfrak a}_i$) is
$\bar\nabla_{(X,0)}$-invariant, for every section $X$ of $B$.  It follows that $\Phi $
intertwines some grading-preserving representation $R$ of $B$ on
$\graded(A)=\graded(TM)\oplus B^0 \oplus (\oplus_{j>0}{\mathfrak a}_j)$ with the
$\bar\nabla$-representation of $B \oplus 0$ on $A$:
\begin{equation*}
  \bar\nabla_{(X, 0)} \Big(\,\Phi(V,C,Z)\,\Big) = \Phi\Big(\,R_X(V, C, Z)\,\Big);\quad X \in B.
\end{equation*}
It's not hard to see that $R$ on the right is the same thing as $R^\nabla $, as defined in
\ref{inflevi} above, under the identification $B \oplus 0 \cong A/A^1$. As a consequence
we can write this as
\begin{equation}
    \bar\nabla_{(X, 0)} \Big(\,\Phi(V,C,Z)\,\Big)=\Phi(R_XV, [X,C], R_X Z),\label{groof}
\end{equation}
where the ``$R$\,'' in $R_XZ$ has the meaning assigned to it in the beginning of the
current discussion, and with
\begin{equation*}
  T(C, V) = R_C V,\quad
  T(C, Z) = R_C Z,\quad
  T(C, C') = [C,C'],
\end{equation*}
for all $C,C'\in\Gamma(B^0)$, $V\in \Gamma(\graded(TM))$,
$Z \in \Gamma(\oplus_{j>0} {\mathfrak a}_j)$.

On the other hand, for any $Y \in \Gamma(\oplus_{j>0}{\mathfrak a}_j)$, we have
$\Phi(0,0,Y)=(0,Y)$, so compatibility Axiom c2 leads to
\begin{align}
  \bar\nabla_{(0, Y)} \Big(\,\Phi(V, C, Z)\,\Big)
  &=\tau\Big(\,\Phi(0, 0, Y),\,\Phi(V, C, Z)\,\Big) =
    \Phi\Big(\,T((0, 0, Y), (V, C, Z))\,\Big)\label{cab0}\\
  &=\Phi\Big(\,(0,0,[Y,Z] - R_CY) + T(Y, V)\,\Big);
    \quad Y \in \Gamma(\oplus_{j>0}{\mathfrak a}_j).\notag
\end{align}
Combining this last with \eqref{groof}, we have, for any
$(X, Y) \in \Gamma(B \oplus_R(\oplus_{j>0} {\mathfrak a}_j))$,
\begin{conditions}\item[{\bfseries S3.}]
  \quad $\bar\nabla_{(X,Y)}\Phi(V, C, Z)
  =\Phi\Big(\,R_X(V, C, Z) + T((0, 0, Y), (V, C, Z))\,\Big)$,
\end{conditions}
whose right-hand side can also be written as
$$\Phi\Big(\,(R_XV, [X,C], [Y,Z] +R_XZ - R_CY) + T(Y, V)\,\Big).$$

The above analysis leads to the characterizations of transitive filtered Cartan geometries
given next.

\subsection{Prolongation: the infinitesimal case}\label{inflevi_}
Suppose that $(B, \oplus_{j>0}{\mathfrak a}_j, R, T)$ is an abstract infinitesimal Levi
structure. The structure $T$ makes $\oplus_{j>0}{\mathfrak a}_j$ into a graded Lie algebra
bundle and the {\df prolongation} of the abstract infinitesimal Levi structure is
the Lie algebroid semi-direct product $A = B \oplus_R(\oplus_{j>0}{\mathfrak a}_j)$. This
is a firmly filtered Lie algebroid with
$A^i = B^i \oplus_R(\oplus_{j\ge\max\{1,i\}}{\mathfrak a}_j)$.

\begin{theorem}[A characterization of transitive infinitesimal filtered Cartan geometries]
  Let $(B, \oplus_{j>0}{\mathfrak a}_j, R, T)$ be an abstract infinitesimal Levi structure,
  $\mathsf{P}$ be an arbitrary section of
  $\graded(T^*\!M)\otimes(\oplus_{j>0}{\mathfrak a}_j)$, $s \colon TM \rightarrow B$ any
  splitting of the anchor of $B$, and $\sigma \colon \graded(TM) \rightarrow TM $ some
  splitting of the filtered manifold $M$. Then:
  \begin{conditions}
  \item The map
    $\Phi \colon \graded(TM) \oplus B^0 \oplus (\oplus_j {\mathfrak a}_j) \rightarrow B
    \oplus_R(\oplus_{j>0}{\mathfrak a}_j)$ defined by {\normalfont S1} is
    invertible. Specifically, if $\pi \colon B \rightarrow B^0$ is defined by
    $\pi(X):=X - s(\#X)$, and if $(X, Y) = \Phi(V, C, Z)$, then $C = \pi X$,
    $V = \sigma^{-1}(\#X)$, and $Z = Y + \mathsf{P}(V)$. \label{chh1}
  \item\label{chh2} The prolongation $A = B \oplus_R(\oplus_{j>0}{\mathfrak a}_j) $ is a
    transitive, infinitesimal, filtered Cartan geometry, with model data $\tau $ defined
    by {\normalfont S2} and Cartan connection $\nabla $ uniquely determined by
    {\normalfont S3}. The corresponding Levi reduction is isomorphic to
    $(B, \oplus_{j>0}{\mathfrak a}_j, R, T)$.
  \item\label{cch2b} For any section $E$ as in \eqrefs{inflevi}{six},
    $\epsilon := \Phi^{-1}(0, E, 0)$ is a Weyl gauge for $A$ compatible with $\tau $ and
    for which $\Phi \colon \graded(A) \rightarrow A$ is the corresponding splitting.
  \item\label{cch3} Every transitive, infinitesimal, filtered Cartan geometry
    $(A, \nabla, \tau)$, with anchor kernel $A^0$, is, up to isomorphism, the prolongation
    of its Levi reduction, with Cartan connection $\nabla $ and model data $\tau $ of the
    form just described.
  \end{conditions}
\end{theorem}
\noindent%
The section $\mathrm P$ is called the {\df Rho tensor}.
\begin{proof}
  It is a triviality that $\Phi $ is injective. A dimension count implies $\Phi$ must be an
  isomorphism. A substitution verifies the rest of \eqref{chh1}.

  That $\tau $, defined by S2, is model data follows from the properties of $T$ posited in
  \eqrefs{inflevi}{chh0} and the definition of the semi-direct product Lie bracket for
  $B^0 \oplus_R(\oplus_{j>0} {\mathfrak a}_j)$.

  The isomorphism $\Phi$ intertwines the representation $R$ of $B$ on
  $\graded(TM) \oplus B^0 \oplus (\oplus_j {\mathfrak a}_j)$ with some representation
  $\rho^{B \oplus 0}$ of $B \oplus 0 \subset A$ on $A$:
  \begin{equation}
    \rho^{B \oplus 0}_{(X,0)}\Phi(V, C, Z) = \Phi\Big(\,R_X((V, C, Z))\,\Big).\label{ret1}
  \end{equation}
  To apply Proposition \ref{constructing} to $A$, with $\tau $ defined by
  S2, and $A'=A^1=0 \oplus (\oplus_{j>0} {\mathfrak a}_j)$, we need to
  establish \eqrefs{constructing}{ext1}. Here this means verifying that
  \begin{equation*}
    \rho^{B \oplus 0}_{(X,0)}\Phi(0, C, Z) = [(X,0), \Phi(0, C, Z)],
  \end{equation*}
  for $X \in \Gamma(B),\,C \in B^0,\,Z \in \Gamma(\oplus_{j>0}{\mathfrak a}_j)$, which is
  an easy computation following from \eqref{ret1}, and the fact that the bracket on the
  right-hand side is the semi-direct product bracket. Similarly, since $\tau $ is defined
  by S2, the properties of $T$ in \eqrefs{inflevi}{chh0} allow one to show that
  \eqrefs{constructing}{ext3} also holds in the present case. We conclude that there
  exists a unique Cartan connection $\nabla $ on $A$, compatible with $\tau $,
  such that
  \begin{equation*}
    \bar\nabla_{(X,Y)} \Phi(V, C, Z) = \rho^{B \oplus 0}_{(X,0)} \Phi (V, C, Z)
      + \tau((0,Y), \Phi(V, C, Z)).
  \end{equation*}
  The formula S3 follows from \eqref{ret1}, S2, and the identity $(0, Y) = \Phi(0, 0,
  Y)$. The last part of \eqref{chh2}, and \eqref{cch2b}, follow by construction. Part
  \eqref{cch3} of the theorem was already established in \ref{consequences}.
\end{proof}

\subsection{Prolongation: the global case}\label{abstract_levi_}
Suppose that $({\mathcal H}, \oplus_{j>0}{\mathfrak a}_j, R, T)$ is an abstract Levi
structure. The vector bundle $\oplus_{j>0} {\mathfrak a}_j$ gets an $R$-invariant graded
Lie algebra bundle structure by restricting $T$. This bundle has a necessarily nilpotent
Lie algebra model, and we let $\exp(\oplus_{j>0}{\mathfrak a}_j)$ denote the nilpotent Lie
group bundle with simply connected fibres that integrates $ \oplus_{j>0}{\mathfrak
  a}_j$. The restriction of $R$ to a representation of ${\mathcal H} $ on
$\oplus_{j>0}{\mathfrak a}_j$, by fibre-wise Lie algebra derivations, integrates to a
representation of ${\mathcal H}$ on $\exp(\oplus_{j>0}{\mathfrak a}_j)$ by fibre-wise Lie
group isomorphisms; denoting this by $R$ also, we have $R_h(\exp(Y))=\exp(R_hY)$, for any
arrow $h \in {\mathcal H}$ beginning at the base point of
$Y \in \oplus_{j>0}{\mathfrak a}_j $, because $\exp$ is a diffeomorphism in this case.

The {\df prolongation} of the Levi structure is the Lie groupoid semi-direct
product ${\mathcal G} = {\mathcal H} \times_R\exp(\oplus_{j>0}{\mathfrak a}_j)$. This is
a filtered Lie groupoid with Lie algebroid $B \oplus_{dR} (\oplus_{j>0}{\mathfrak a}_j)$,
the prolongation of Levi structure's infinitesimalization.

Additionally, the representation $\adjoint^T$ of the nilpotent Lie algebra bundle
$\oplus_{j>0}{\mathfrak a}_j$ on
$\graded(TM) \oplus B^0 \oplus (\oplus_{j>0}{\mathfrak a}_j)$ integrates to a
representation of the Lie group bundle $\exp(\oplus_{j>0}{\mathfrak a}_j)$ on
$\graded(TM) \oplus B^0 \oplus (\oplus_{j>0}{\mathfrak a}_j)$. We denote this
representation by $\Adjoint^T$.

\begin{theorem}[A characterization of transitive filtered Cartan geometries]\mbox{}\newline
  Let $({\mathcal H}, \oplus_{j>0}{\mathfrak a}_j, R, T)$ be an abstract Levi structure,
  $B$ the Lie algebroid of ${\mathcal H} $, $\mathsf{P}$ an arbitrary section of
  $\graded(T^*\!M)\otimes(\oplus_{j>0}{\mathfrak a}_j)$, $s \colon TM \rightarrow B$ any
  splitting of the anchor of $B$, and $\sigma \colon \graded(TM) \rightarrow TM $ some
  splitting of the filtered manifold $M$. Then:
  \begin{conditions}
  \item\label{chh01} The map
    $\Phi \colon \graded(TM) \oplus B^0 \oplus (\oplus_j {\mathfrak a}_j) \rightarrow B
    \oplus_{dR}(\oplus_{j>0}{\mathfrak a}_j)$ defined by {\normalfont S1} is
    invertible.
  \item\label{chh02} The prolongation
    ${\mathcal G}  = {\mathcal H} \times_R\exp(\oplus_{j>0}{\mathfrak a}_j) $ is a transitive,
    filtered Cartan geometry, with model data $\tau $ defined by
    {\normalfont S2} and Cartan connection $D$ uniquely determined by
  \item[{\normalfont\bfseries S3$^\prime$.}]  \vspace{0.3\baselineskip} \quad
    $\bar D_{(h,k)}\Phi(V, C, Z) = \Phi(\Adjoint^T_k(R_hV, \Adjoint_h C, R_h Z))$.
    \vspace{0.3\baselineskip}\newline The corresponding Levi reduction is isomorphic to
    $({\mathcal H}, \oplus_{j>0}{\mathfrak a}_j, R, T)$.
  \item\label{chh02b} For any section $E$ as in \eqrefs{abstract_levi}{five},
    $\epsilon = \Phi^{-1}(0, E, 0)$ is a Weyl gauge for ${\mathcal G} $ compatible with
    $\tau$ and for which $\Phi \colon \graded(A) \rightarrow A$ is the corresponding
    splitting.
  \item\label{cch03}
    \vspace{0.5\baselineskip}
    Every transitive, filtered, Cartan geometry
    $({\mathcal G}, D, \tau)$, with Lie algebroid $A$ and anchor kernel $A^0$, is, up to
    isomorphism, the prolongation of some abstract Levi structure, with Cartan
    connection $D $ and model data $\tau $ of the form just described.
  \end{conditions}
\end{theorem}
\begin{proof}
  The preceding infinitesimal result, Theorem \ref{inflevi_}, applies with $R$ there
  replaced with $dR$. In particular, \eqref{chh01} is just a restatement of
  \eqrefs{inflevi_}{chh1}.

  The isomorphism $\Phi$ intertwines the representation $R$ of ${\mathcal H} $ on
  $\graded(TM) \oplus B^0 \oplus (\oplus_j {\mathfrak a}_j)$ with some representation
  $\rho^{{\mathcal H} \times \identity}$ on
  ${\mathcal H} \times \identity \subset {\mathcal G} $ on
  $A = B\oplus_{dR}(\oplus_{j>0}{\mathfrak a}_j) $:
  \begin{equation}
    \rho^{{\mathcal H} \times \identity}_{(h,\identity)}\Phi(V, C, Z) =
      \Phi\Big(\,R_h((V, C, Z))\,\Big).\label{ret01}
  \end{equation}
  To apply the global case of Proposition \ref{constructing} to ${\mathcal G}$, with
  $\tau $ defined by S2, and
  ${\mathcal G}'=\identity \times \exp(\oplus_{j>0} {\mathfrak a}_j)$, we
  need to establish \eqrefs{constructing}{pony4}. Here this means verifying that
  \begin{equation*}
    \rho^{{\mathcal H} \times \identity}_{(h,\identity)}\Phi(0, C, Z) =
    \Adjoint_{(h,\identity)}\Phi(0, C, Z),
  \end{equation*}
  for each arrow $h \in {\mathcal G}$ beginning as some $m \in M$, $C \in B^0|_m$,
  $Z \in \oplus_{j>0}{\mathfrak a}_j|_m$. With the help of \eqref{ret01}, and the
  definition of $\Adjoint$ for semi-direct products, this is readily checked. We conclude
  that there exists a unique Cartan connection $D$ on ${\mathcal G} $, at least weakly
  compatible with $\tau$, such that
  \begin{equation}
    \label{mask1}
    \bar D_{(h,k)}\Phi(V, C, Z) =
       \Adjoint^\tau_{(\identity,k)}\rho^{{\mathcal H}\times \identity}_{(h,\identity)}\Phi(V, C, Z),
  \end{equation}
  where $\Adjoint^\tau$ is the representation of
  $\identity \times \exp(\oplus_{j>0}{\mathfrak a}_j) \subset {\mathcal G} $ on $A$
  integrating the representation $\adjoint^\tau$ of
  $A^1=0\oplus (\oplus_{j>0}{\mathfrak a}_j)$ on $A$ defined by
  $\adjoint^\tau_{(0,Y)}W = \tau((0,Y), W)$. By the definition of $\tau $, the isomorphism
  $\Phi $ intertwines the representation $\adjoint^\tau$ of $A^1$ with the representation
  $Y \mapsto T((0,0,Y),\,\cdot\,)$ of $\oplus_{j>0}{\mathfrak a}_j$. Consequently, as
  $\exp(\oplus_{j>0}{\mathfrak a}_j)$ has connected fibres, $\Phi $ intertwines the
  representations $\Adjoint^\tau$ and $\Adjoint^T$:
  \begin{equation}
    \label{mask2}
    \Adjoint^\tau_{(\identity, k)}\Phi(V, C, Z) = \Phi(\Adjoint^T_k((V, C, Z)).
  \end{equation}
  Combining \eqref{ret01}, \eqref{mask1} and \eqref{mask2}, we obtain S3${}^\prime$. The
  last part of \eqref{chh02}, and \eqref{chh02b}, follow by construction.

  It is easy to see that the infinitesimalization $\nabla $ of $D$ must be the Cartan
  connection delivered by Theorem \ref{inflevi_}. Since $\nabla $ is {\em strongly}
  compatible with $\tau $, $D$ is also.

  Turning to \eqref{cch03}, let $({\mathcal G}, D, \tau)$ be a transitive, filtered, Cartan
  geometry with Lie algebroid $A$ and anchor kernel $A^0$. By Theorem \eqrefs{weyl2}{pr5},
  we may suppose, without loss of generality, that
  ${\mathcal G} = {\mathcal H} \times_R\exp(\oplus_{j>0}{\mathfrak a}_j)$, for some
  filtered Lie groupoid ${\mathcal H}$ and graded Lie algebra bundle
  $\oplus_{j>0}{\mathfrak a}_j$, where ${\mathcal H} $ acts on
  $\oplus_{j>0}{\mathfrak a}_j$ by grading-preserving fibre-wise derivations, an action
  that integrates to an action of ${\mathcal H} $ on $\exp(\oplus_{j>0}{\mathfrak a}_j)$
  by fibre-wise Lie group isomorphisms, both actions to be denoted $R$. Moreover, the Lie
  algebroid $B$ of ${\mathcal H} $ will satisfy $B^j=0$ for $j>0$ and, by our hypotheses
  on $A$, $B$ is transitive with $B^0$ being the anchor kernel.

  Evidently, $A$ is identifiable with $B \oplus_{dR}(\oplus_{j>0}{\mathfrak a}_j)$,
  which the infinitesimalization $\nabla $ of $D$ makes into a transitive, infinitesimal,
  filtered Cartan geometry. Consequently, the analysis of \ref{consequences} applies, with
  $R$ in that analysis replaced with $dR$. Define ${\mathfrak a}'_j $, $j>0$, and $\Phi$
  as in that analysis. Then $\tau $ can be recovered from $T=\graded_0(\tau)$ according to
  S2, and, according to Proposition
  \eqrefs{model_data_gradings}{uu4}, the grading $A=\oplus_i {\mathfrak a}'_i$ (there
  denoted $\oplus_i {\mathfrak a}_i$) is $\bar D_{(h,\identity)}$-invariant, for every
  $h \in {\mathcal H} $. It follows that $\Phi $ intertwines some grading-preserving
  representation $R$ of ${\mathcal H}$ on
  $\graded(A)=\graded(TM)\oplus B^0 \oplus (\oplus_{j>0}{\mathfrak a}_j)$ with the
  $\bar D$-representation of ${\mathcal H} \times \identity$ on $A$:
  \begin{equation}
    \bar D_{(h, \identity)} \Phi(V,C,Z) = \Phi\Big(\,R_h(V, C, Z)\,\Big);\quad h \in {\mathcal H}.
  \end{equation}
  Since $\Phi(0, C, Z) = (C, Z)$ and $\bar D $ is just the canonical
  representation on sections of $A^0$, $R$ must extend the canonical representation of
  ${\mathcal H}$ on $\graded(A^0) = B^0 \oplus(\oplus_{j>0} {\mathfrak a}_j) $, which
  gives
  \begin{equation}
    \bar D_{(h, \identity)} \Phi(V,C,Z)\Phi(R_hV, \Adjoint_hC, R_h Z);\quad h \in {\mathcal H},\label{cab1}
  \end{equation}
  where the ``$R$'' in $R_hZ$ has the meaning given at the beginning of this discussion.

  On the other hand, \eqrefs{consequences}{cab0} implies
  \begin{equation*}
    \bar\nabla_{(0,Y)} \Phi(\xi) = \Phi(\adjoint^T_Y \xi),\qquad
    Y \in \Gamma(\oplus_{j>0}{\mathfrak a}_j),\,\xi \in \Gamma(\graded(A)).
  \end{equation*}
  Because $\exp(\oplus_{j>0}{\mathfrak a}_j)$ has simply-connected fibres, this
  intertwining by $\Phi $ of infinitesimal actions is an intertwining of their
  corresponding globalizations:
  \begin{equation}
    \label{cab2}
    \bar D_{(\identity, k)} \Phi(V, C, Z) = \Phi(\Adjoint^T_k(V,C, Z)).
  \end{equation}
  The formula S3$^\prime$ follows from \eqref{cab1} and \eqref{cab2} and the identity
  $(h, k) = (\identity, k)(h, \identity)$ for the semi-direct product.
\end{proof}

% \subsection{Prolongation as functor}\label{functor}
% Here we argue that prolongation is a suitable functor. This section is fairly formal and
% the reader may find it easier to reproduce the obvious definitions herself than to parse
% the details, which are included here for completeness.

% A morphism of filtered Lie algebroids $q \colon A \rightarrow \tilde A$ is a Lie algebroid
% morphism respecting the filtrations: $q(A^j) \subset \tilde A^j$. A morphism of filtered
% Lie groupoids $Q \colon {\mathcal G} \rightarrow \tilde {\mathcal G} $ is a Lie groupoid
% morphism whose infinitesimalization $q=dQ \colon A \rightarrow \tilde A$ is a morphism of
% firmly filtered Lie algebroids. We obtain the category of {\em firmly} filtered Lie
% algebroids or Lie groupoids by simply restricting the class of morphisms to those whose
% source and target are firmly filtered objects.

% A morphism of abstract infinitesimal Levi structures
% $(B, \oplus_{j>0} {\mathfrak a}_j, R, T)$ and
% $(\tilde B, \oplus_{j>0} \tilde{\mathfrak a}_j, \tilde R, \tilde T)$ consists of a pair
% $(q, \omega)$, where $q \colon B \rightarrow \tilde B$ is morphism of filtered Lie
% algebroids and
% $\omega \colon \oplus_{j>0}{\mathfrak a}_j \rightarrow \oplus_{j>0}\tilde{\mathfrak a}_j$
% a morphism of graded vector bundles, such that induced
% morphims of graded vector bundles
% \begin{gather*}
%   (q, \omega)_* \colon \graded(TM)\oplus B^0 \oplus (\oplus_{j>0}{\mathfrak a}_j)
%      \rightarrow \graded(TM)\oplus \tilde B^0 \oplus (\oplus_{j>0}\tilde{\mathfrak a}_j)\\
%   (V, C, Z) \mapsto (\graded_0(q^\vee)(V), qC, \omega Z)
% \end{gather*}
% is: (i) a morphism of Lie algebra bundles, with respect to the brackets $T$ and
% $\tilde T$; and (ii) an intertwining of the representations $R$ and $\tilde R$. Here
% $q^\vee \colon TM \rightarrow TM$ is the filtration-preserving morphism covered by $q$, in
% the sense that $\# \circ q = q^\vee \circ \#$. A morphism of abstract Levi structures
% $({\mathcal H}, \oplus_{j>0}{\mathfrak a}_j, R, T)$ and
% $(\tilde {\mathcal H}, \oplus_{j>0}\tilde{\mathfrak a}_j, \tilde R, \tilde T)$ is a pair
% $(Q, \omega)$, where $Q \colon {\mathcal H} \rightarrow \tilde {\mathcal H} $ is morphism
% of filtered Lie groupoids and
% $\omega \colon \oplus_{j>0}{\mathfrak a}_j \rightarrow \oplus_{j>0}\tilde{\mathfrak a}_j$
% a morphism of graded vector bundles, such that: (i) $(dQ, \omega)$ is a morphism of the
% corresponding abstract infinitesimal Levi structures; and (ii) $(dQ, \omega)_*$
% intertwines the (global) representations $R$ and $\tilde R$.

% The {\df abstract prolongation} of a morphism $(q, \omega)$ of abstract infinitesimal Levi
% structures as above is the morphism of firmly filtered Lie algebroids
% \begin{gather*}
%   B \oplus_R (\oplus_{j>0}{\mathfrak a}_j)
%     \rightarrow \tilde B \oplus_{\tilde R} (\oplus_{j>0}\tilde{\mathfrak a}_j) \\
%   (X, Y) \mapsto (qX, \omega Y).
% \end{gather*}
% For the morphism $(Q, \omega)$ of abstract Levi structures described above, we can
% integrate the morphism of Lie algebra bundles
% $\omega \colon (\oplus_{j>0}{\mathfrak a}_j, T) \rightarrow (\oplus_{j>0}\tilde{\mathfrak
%   a}_j, \tilde T) $ to a morphism of Lie group bundles
% $\Omega \colon \exp(\oplus_{j>0}{\mathfrak a}_j) \rightarrow
% \exp(\oplus_{j>0}\tilde{\mathfrak a}_j)$, and the {\df prolongation} of
% $(Q, \omega)$ is then the morphism of firmly filtered Lie groupoids,
% \begin{align*}
%   {\mathcal H} \times _R \exp(\oplus_{j>0}{\mathfrak a}_j)
%     &\rightarrow \tilde {\mathcal H}  \times_{\tilde R} \exp(\oplus_{j>0}\tilde{\mathfrak a}_j) \\
%   (h, k) &\mapsto  (Q(h), \Omega (k)).
% \end{align*}

% With these definitions, one readily establishes the following facts:
% \begin{proposition}
%   Abstract prolongation is a functor from the category of abstract infinitesimal or global
%   Levi geometries to the category of firmly filtered Lie algebroids, resp., Lie
%   groupoids.
% \end{proposition}

% \begin{corollary}
%   If two abstract infinitesimal or global Levi structures are isomorphic, then so are their
%   corresponding prolongations.
% \end{corollary}


\refreshpage
\section{Deforming model data and Cartan connections}\label{deform}
We need a way to relate different choices of model data in a filtered Cartan geometry
using transformations of the underlying Lie algebroid or integrating Lie
groupoid. Proposition \ref{deformations} below addresses this need.

\subsection{$\psi$-deformations}\label{deformations}
Let $A$ be a Lie algebroid. For each $\psi \in \Gamma(T^*\!M \otimes A) $, define
$\psi_{TM}:TM \rightarrow TM$ by
\begin{equation}\label{opal1}
  \psi_{TM} V = V + \#\,\psi\,V,
\end{equation}
and define $\Adjoint_\psi \colon A \rightarrow A$ by
\begin{equation}
  \label{opal2a}
  \Adjoint_\psi X = X + \psi(\#X).
\end{equation}
Here $\# \colon A \rightarrow TM$ denotes the anchor. The natural context giving rise to
these definitions is provided in \ref{kernel}. For the moment, it suffices to observe
that: (i) If $\psi_{TM}$ is invertible,
then so is $\Adjoint_\psi$, with
\begin{equation}
  \label{opal2}
  \Adjoint_\psi^{-1} = \Adjoint_{-\psi\circ(\psi_{TM})^{-1}};
\end{equation}
and (ii) If $A$ is filtered and transitive and $\psi$ is homogeneous of degree one, i.e.,
$\psi(A^k) \subset A^{k+1}$ for any $k$, then $\psi_{TM}$ is invertible, because in that
case $\psi_{TM}$ is filtration-preserving with
$\graded_0(\psi_{TM})=\identity$.

\begin{lemma}
  Let $A$ be a filtered Lie algebroid and $q \colon A \rightarrow A$ a vector bundle
  isomorphism covering the identity such that $q - \identity$ is homogeneous of degree
  $l\ge 1$. Then the push-forward $\tau' = q_*\tau $ of any model data $\tau $ on $A$
  compatible with the filtration is also compatible with the filtration, and satisfies
  $\graded_0(\tau')=\graded_0(\tau)$. Assuming $A^0$ is the anchor kernel of $A$, $\tau'$
  is also model data.
\end{lemma}
\begin{proof}
  Since $q$ will be filtration-preserving, so is $q^{-1}$, which shows $\tau' $ is
  compatible with the filtration. If $qX = X + Y$, then $q^{-1}X = X - q^{-1}(Y)$, and we
  can therefore see that $q^{-1} - \identity$ is also homogeneous of degree $l$. The
  push-forward is defined by $\tau'(X, Y) = q \tau (q^{-1}X, q^{-1}Y)$, and, with the
  preceding observations in hand, checking $\graded_0(\tau') = \graded_0(\tau)$ is
  straightforward. The last statement holds because $\tau $ is model data and $q, q^{-1}$
  are filtration-preserving.
\end{proof}

If $\tau $ is compatible with the filtration of a filtered Lie algebroid $A$, with anchor
kernel $A^0$, then, assuming $\psi $ is homogeneous of degree $l \ge 1$, the lemma shows
that $\tau' = (\Adjoint_\psi)_* \tau $ is model data with
$\graded_0(\tau') = \graded_0(\tau)$. Conversely, we have:
\begin{proposition}
  Let $A$ be a transitive filtered Lie algebroid with anchor kernel $A^0$, and $\tau$,
  $\tau'$ model data compatible with the filtration. Assume $T := \graded_0(\tau)$ admits
  a fibre-wise grading section $E$, and that $\graded_0(\tau') = T$. Then:
  \begin{conditions}
  \item\label{saturn1} There exists a unique $\psi \in \Gamma(T^*\!M \otimes A)$,
    necessarily homogeneous of degree one, such that $\tau' = (\Adjoint_\psi)_*\tau$.
  \item\label{saturn2} If $\tau $ is compatible with some infinitesimal Cartan connection
    $\nabla $, then $\tau'$ is compatible with the infinitesimal Cartan connection
    $\nabla'$ defined implicitly by
    $$\bar\nabla'_XY = \Adjoint_\psi (\bar\nabla_X(\Adjoint_\psi^{-1}Y)).$$
  \item \label{saturn3} If ${\mathcal G} $ is a Lie groupoid integrating $A$ and $\tau $
    is compatible with some Cartan connection $D$, then $\tau'$ is compatible with the
    Cartan connection $D'$ defined implicitly by
    $$\bar D'_gX = \Adjoint_{\psi(gm)}\bar D_g \Adjoint_{\psi(m)}^{-1}X,$$ for each arrow
    $g \in {\mathcal G} $ beginning at some $m \in M$, and each $X \in A|_{m}$, and whose
    infinitesimalization is $\nabla'$ above,
  \item\label{saturn5} If $({\mathcal G}, D, \tau)$ is a transitive filtered Cartan
    geometry, then $({\mathcal G}, D', \tau')$ is another transitive filtered Cartan
    geometry with the same Levi reduction. An analogous statement holds in the
    infinitesimal case.
  \end{conditions}

\end{proposition}
%

When $\tau'=(\Adjoint)_*\tau$, and $D'$ and $\nabla'$ are defined (implicitly) by
\eqref{saturn3} and \eqref{saturn2}, then the primed quantities will be called the {\df
  $\psi$-deformations} of $\tau $, $D$ and $\nabla $. The proof of the proposition is
given in \ref{existence_deformations}--\ref{same_levi} below. In \ref{gauge_transforms} we
connect $\psi$-deformations to Weyl gauge transformations.

\subsection{The existence of deformations}\label{existence_deformations}
The existence part of Proposition \eqrefs{deformations}{saturn1} has an elementary proof
proceeding as follows. Let $\tau$ and $\tau'$ be model data as in the proposition and fix
a lift $\epsilon \in \Gamma(A^0)$ through $A^0 \rightarrow A^0/A^1$ of $E$. Then, as we
have described in \ref{splittings}, we get two corresponding splittings
$\Phi, \Phi' \colon \graded(A) \rightarrow A $ of the Lie algebra bundles $(A, \tau)$ and
$(A, \tau')$. By definition, we have $\Phi_*T=\tau $ and $\Phi'_*T= \tau'$, and, because
$\tau $ and $\tau' $ agree on $A^0$ (by the definition of model data)
$\Phi' \circ \Phi^{-1}$ is the identity on $A^0$. It follows from the transitivity of $A$
that $\tau' = \Psi_* \tau$, where $\Psi := \Phi' \circ \Phi^{-1}$ satisfies
$\Psi(X) = X + \psi (\#X)=\Adjoint_\psi X$ for some vector bundle morphism
$\psi \colon TM \rightarrow A$.

Also following from the definition of splittings, we have, for any $X \in \Gamma(A^k)$ and
$k \in {\mathbb Z}$,
\begin{gather}
  X \equiv \Phi(\graded_k(X)) \modulo A^{k+1},\label{opal3}\\
  \Phi'(\graded_k(X)) \equiv X \modulo A^{k+1}.\label{opal4}
\end{gather}
From \eqref{opal3} we conclude that
$(\Phi' \circ \Phi^{-1})(X) \equiv \Phi'(\graded_k(X)) \modulo A^{k+1}$, because
$\Phi' \circ \Phi^{-1}$ is filtration-preserving. Combining this with \eqref{opal4}, we
conclude that $\Phi' \circ \Phi^{-1}(X) \equiv X \modulo A^{k+1}$, i.e., $\psi$ is
homogeneous of degree one.

\subsection{The kernel of $J^1 {\mathcal G} \rightarrow {\mathcal G} $}\label{kernel}

Let $A$ be any integrable Lie algebroid. The sections $\psi$ of $T^*\!M \otimes A$ for
which $\psi_{TM}$ are invertible are sections of an open neighborhood of the zero section
of $T^*\!M \otimes A$ that we denote $\model$. The proposition below shows that this set
is a model for the kernel of the projection $J^1 {\mathcal G} \rightarrow {\mathcal G} $
for {\em any} Lie groupoid ${\mathcal G} $ integrating $A$. In particular, it is a totally
intransitive Lie groupoid (a bundle of Lie groups). We now describe the corresponding
groupoid structure directly.

The zero section of $T^*\!M \otimes A$ constitutes the set of identity elements of
$\model$. Multiplication is given by
\begin{equation}
  \label{clost}
  \psi \varphi = \psi + \varphi + \psi \circ \# \circ \varphi = \varphi + \psi \circ \varphi_{TM}.
\end{equation}
Inversion is given by
\begin{equation*}
  \psi \mapsto  -\psi \circ (\psi_{TM})^{-1}.
\end{equation*}
A convenient consequence we mention in passing is the formula
\begin{equation}
  \label{clost2}
  \psi \varphi^{-1} = (\psi - \varphi)\circ \varphi_{TM}^{-1}.
\end{equation}
With respect to these groupoid structures, the map
$$\psi \mapsto \psi_{TM} \colon \model \rightarrow
\automorphism({TM})$$ is a morphism of totally intransitive Lie groupoids and the
commutative kernel consists of those $\psi \colon TM \rightarrow A$ with image lying in
the kernel of the anchor.

The reader will readily see that the maps defined by \eqrefs{kernel}{opal1} and
\eqrefs{kernel}{opal2a} define representations of $\model$ on $A$ and $TM$ respectively.
With respect to these representations the anchor is equivariant:
$\#\Adjoint_\psi X = \psi_{TM}\#X$.

Although the proposition below provides useful context, the proof of Proposition
\ref{deformations} will not actually require it. However, the result is needed in Appendix
\ref{rut}.

Let ${\mathcal G} $ be any Lie groupoid with Lie algebroid $A$. Represent elements of
$J^1 {\mathcal G} $ by maps tangent to some local bisection of ${\mathcal G} $, i.e., by
certain vector space morphisms $T_{m}M \rightarrow T_g {\mathcal G} $, where
$g \in {\mathcal G} $ is some arrow beginning at some $m \in M$. Recall that the adjoint
representation for a Lie groupoid ${\mathcal G} $ is actually a representation of
$J^1 {\mathcal G} $ on $A$ \cite{Blaom_16b}, and that $J^1 {\mathcal G} $ also acts
naturally on $TM$. Both representations are denoted $\Adjoint$, and with respect to these
the anchor is equivariant.

\begin{proposition}[\cite{Blaom_16b}]
  The map $\psi \mapsto \varcheck \psi \colon \model \rightarrow J^1 G$, defined by
  $\varcheck \psi V = V + \psi\,V$, is a Lie groupoid morphism and embedding, whose image
  is the kernel of the natural projection $J^1 G \rightarrow G$.\footnote{\cite{Blaom_16b}
    adopts a different sign convention for the embedding and definition of $\model$.} This
  map is equivariant with respect to the natural representations of both groupoids on $A$
  and $TM$: $\Adjoint_{\varcheck\psi} V = \psi_{TM}V$,
  $\Adjoint_{\varcheck\psi} X = \Adjoint_\psi X$, for $V \in {T_{m}M}$, $X \in A|_m$, and
  $m \in M$.
\end{proposition}

\subsection{The deformed Cartan connections}
In passing, let us explain how the deformed connections $\nabla'$ and $D'$ appearing in
Proposition \ref{deformations} arise very naturally. Recall that a Cartan connection $D$
is the $n$-plane field determined by some Lie groupoid right-inverse
$S \colon {\mathcal G} \rightarrow J^1 {\mathcal G}$ for the natural projection
$ J^1 {\mathcal G} \rightarrow {\mathcal G}$. Given some $\psi \in \Gamma(\model)$, we
may, according to the preceding proposition, view it as bisection of $J^1 {\mathcal G} $
and obtain, via conjugation, a corresponding automorphism $K_\psi$ of $J^1 {\mathcal G}$,
sending an arrow $\mu \in J^1_g {\mathcal G} $, beginning at some $m \in M$ with
projection $g \in {\mathcal G}$, to $\varcheck{\psi(gm)}\mu (\varcheck{\psi(m)})^{-1}$. It
is easy to see that $S':=K_\psi \circ S \colon {\mathcal G} \rightarrow J^1 {\mathcal G} $
is another right-inverse, defining a new Cartan connection $D'$. From the definition of
the corresponding representations $\bar D$ and $\bar D'$, one immediately derives the
formula in \eqrefs{deformations}{saturn3}.

Now $\bar\nabla $ is the infinitesimalization of the representation $\bar D $, and it
therefore follows from the formula in \eqrefs{deformations}{saturn3}, and a simple
computation, that the infinitesimalization $\bar\nabla'$ of $\bar D'$ is given by the
formula in \eqrefs{deformations}{saturn2}.

We now return to the proof of Proposition \ref{deformations}. Regardless of whether $A$ is
integrated by some Lie groupoid, the formula for $\bar\nabla'$ given in
\eqrefs{deformations}{saturn2} must define an infinitesimal Cartan connection, by the
characterization of such connections given in Proposition \ref{hsd}, which applies because
we assume $A$ is transitive. The main point here is that \eqrefs{deformations}{saturn2}
indeed defines a representation. The details are not difficult and are left to the
reader. It is a simple computation to show that $\tau' = (\Adjoint_\psi)_*\tau $ must be
$\bar\nabla'$-invariant ($\nabla'$-compatible) whenever $\tau $ is $\bar\nabla$-invariant
($\nabla$-compatible).

Similarly, the formula for $\bar D'$ given in \eqrefs{deformations}{saturn3} must define a
global Cartan connection, by the characterization of such connections given in Proposition
\ref{cartan}, and checking that $\tau' = (\Adjoint_\psi)_*\tau $ must be
$\bar D'$-invariant ($D'$-compatible) whenever $\tau $ is $\bar D$-invariant
($D$-compatible) is a simple computation.

This completes the proof of parts \eqref{saturn2} and \eqref{saturn3} of Proposition
\ref{deformations}.

\subsection{The uniqueness of $\psi$-deformations}\label{deformation_uniqueness}
Having seen that $\psi \mapsto \Adjoint_\psi $ defines a representation of $\model$ on
$A$, to prove the uniqueness of $\psi $ in Proposition \eqrefs{deformations}{saturn1}, it
evidently suffices to show that $(\Adjoint_\psi)^*\tau = \tau$ implies $\psi = 0$,
whenever $\psi $ is homogeneous of degree one, because $\Adjoint_0=\identity$.

Let $\tau $ and $E$ be as in Proposition \ref{deformations} and
$\psi \colon TM \rightarrow A$ be homogeneous of degree one. If we temporarily write
$\hat \psi(X) = \psi(\#X)$, then $(\Adjoint_\psi)^*\tau = \tau$ means
\begin{equation*}
  \tau(\hat\psi X, Y) + \tau(X,\hat\psi Y) + \tau(\hat\psi X, \hat\psi Y) = \hat\psi \tau(X, Y),
\end{equation*}
for all $X, Y \in \Gamma(A)$. In particular, if $\epsilon $ is any lift of $E$ through
$A^0 \rightarrow A^0/A^1$, then
\begin{equation}\label{opal5}
  \tau(\hat\psi X, \epsilon) = \hat\psi(\tau(X, \epsilon)); \qquad X \in \Gamma(A).
\end{equation}
For an inductive argument, suppose $\psi $ (and therefore $\hat\psi $) is homogeneous of
degree $l\ge 1$. Then \eqref{opal5} gives
$T(\graded_l(\hat\psi)\xi, E) = \graded_l(\hat\psi)(T(\xi, E))$, for any
$\xi \in \graded(A)$. In particular, if $j < 0$ and $\xi \in \graded(A)_j$, then
$(j+l) \graded_l(\hat\psi)\xi = j \graded_l(\hat\psi)\xi $, which can only be true if
$\graded_l(\hat\psi)\xi =0$. Since this last is trivially true in the other cases
$j\ge 0$, we conclude that $\hat\psi$, and hence $\psi $, is homogeneous of degree
$l+1$. Induction on $l$ shows $\psi = 0$. This completes the proof of Proposition
\eqrefs{deformations}{saturn1}.

\subsection{Levi reductions are unchanged by $\psi $-deformations}\label{same_levi}
Conclusion \eqrefs{deformations}{saturn5} follows fairly easily from the definitions and
Lemma \ref{deformations}, applied to $q=\Adjoint_\psi $, and is left to the reader.

\subsection{Weyl gauge transformations and $\psi$-deformations}\label{gauge_transforms}

If we use a Weyl gauge transformation to transform model data, then we can say something
about the $\psi$-deformation realizing the same change:

\begin{proposition}
  Let $A$ be a transitive filtered Lie algebroid with anchor kernel $A^0$, $\tau$ model
  data compatible with the filtration, and assume $T := \graded_0(\tau)$ admits a
  fibre-wise grading section $E$. Then for any $Z \in \Gamma(A^l)$, $l \ge 1$, there
  exists unique $\psi \in \Gamma(T^*\!M \otimes A)$, homogeneous of degree $l$, such
  that $(e^{-\adjoint_Z})_*\tau = (\Adjoint_\psi)_* \tau$. In that case, for any
  integer $k < 0$,
  \begin{equation}
    \label{opal7}
    \psi(\#X) \equiv \tau(Z, X) \modulo A^{k+l+1};\qquad X \in \Gamma(A^k).
  \end{equation}
\end{proposition}
%
\begin{remark}
After introducing the operator $\partial$ in \ref{curv_deform}, we will be able to express
\eqref{opal7} as $\graded_l(\psi) = \partial \graded_l(Z)$.
\end{remark}
%
\begin{proof}
  By Proposition \ref{deformations}, there exists unique
  $\psi \in \Gamma(T^*\!M \otimes A)$ such that
  $(e^{-\adjoint_Z})_*\tau = (\Adjoint_\psi)_* \tau$, but {\em a priori} we know only that
  $\psi $ is homogeneous of degree {\em one}. Fixing some lift $\epsilon $ through
  $A^0 \rightarrow A^0/A^1$ of $E$, we obtain corresponding splittings
  $A = \oplus_j {\mathfrak a}_j$ and $A = \oplus_j {\mathfrak a}_j'$ with respect to the
  Lie algebra bundle structures $\tau $ and $\tau':=(\Adjoint_\psi)_*\tau$,
  respectively. It is not too hard to see it suffices to prove \eqref{opal7} under the
  seemingly more restrictive hypothesis $X \in {\mathfrak a}_k$, in which case
  \begin{equation}
    \label{opal0}
    \Adjoint_\psi X \in {\mathfrak a}_k'.
  \end{equation}
  Since $\Adjoint_\psi(X) = X + \psi(\#X)$ and $\psi$ is homogeneous of degree one, we may
  define $X_k:=X$ and have $\psi(\#X) = \sum_{m\ge k + 1} X_m$ and
  $\Adjoint_\psi(X)=\sum_{m\ge k} X_m$, for some
  $X_{k+1} \in {\mathfrak a}_{k+1}, X_{k+2}\in {\mathfrak a}_{k+2},$ etc., finite in
  number. These preliminaries set up a simple but tedious computation, tracking the
  relevant degrees of homogeneity. For completeness, details now follow.

  The requirement \eqref{opal0} gives
  \begin{equation}
    \label{opal8}
    \tau'\big(\epsilon, \sum_{m\ge k}X_m\big) = k\sum_{m\ge k}X_m.
  \end{equation}
  We have
  \begin{gather*}
     e^{\adjoint_Z}\epsilon=\epsilon +[Z, \epsilon] + \frac{1}{2}[Z,[Z,\epsilon]] + \cdots\\
       =\epsilon +\tau(Z, \epsilon) + \frac{1}{2}\tau(Z,\tau(Z,\epsilon)) + \cdots\enspace.
  \end{gather*}
  On the other hand, we may write $Z = Z_l + Z^{l+1}$, for some
  $Z_l \in \Gamma({\mathfrak a}_l)$ and $Z^{l+1} \in \Gamma(A^l)$, and since
  $\tau(Z_l, \epsilon) = - lZ_l$, it's not hard to see that see that
  $e^{\adjoint_Z}\epsilon = \epsilon - l Z + \delta $, for some
  $\delta \in \Gamma(A^{l+1})$.

  Firmness of the filtration of $A$, and the expansion of $e^{\adjoint_Z}$, ensure that
  \begin{equation}
    \label{ruby0}
     e^{\adjoint_Z}Y \equiv Y \modulo A^l,
  \end{equation}
  where here $Y \in \Gamma(A)$ is completely arbitrary. Regarding the left-hand side of
  \eqref{opal8}, we now compute
  \begin{gather}
    \tau'\big(\epsilon, \sum_{m\ge k}X_m\big) =
    e^{-\adjoint_Z}\tau\Big(e^{\adjoint_Z}\epsilon,
    e^{\adjoint_Z}\big(\sum_{m\ge k}X_m\big)\Big)\notag\\
    = e^{-\adjoint_Z}\tau\big(\epsilon - lZ + \delta, \sum_{m\ge k}X_m\big) +
      e^{-\adjoint_Z}\tau(\epsilon - lZ + \delta, W),\label{ruby5}
  \end{gather}
  where $W := e^{-\adjoint_Z}(\sum_{m\ge k}X_m) - \sum_{m\ge k}X_m$, which lies in $A^l$,
  by \eqref{ruby0}. In particular, the second term on the right-hand side of \eqref{ruby5}
  must lie in $A^l$ also. So, developing \eqref{ruby5} further, we have
  \begin{gather*}
    \tau'\big(\epsilon, \sum_{m\ge k}X_m\big) \equiv
    e^{-\adjoint_Z}\tau\big(\epsilon - lZ + \delta, \sum_{m\ge k}X_m\big) \modulo A^l \\
    \equiv  e^{-\adjoint_Z}\Big(\,\sum_{m\ge k}m X_m -
      l\sum_{m\ge k}\tau(Z, X_m) + \sum_{m\ge k}\tau(\delta, X_m)\,\Big) \modulo A^l\\
      \equiv \sum_{m\ge k}m X_m - l\sum_{m\ge k}\tau(Z, X_m) +
      \sum_{m\ge k}\tau(\delta, X_m)\,\modulo A^l,
  \end{gather*}
  where in the last step we have again applied identity \eqref{ruby0}. Combining this with
  \eqref{opal8}, we conclude
  \begin{equation}
    \label{ruby6}
    \sum_{m>k}(m-k) X_m \equiv l\sum_{m\ge k}\tau(Z, X_m) + \sum_{m\ge k}\tau(\delta, X_m)\modulo A^l.
  \end{equation}
  Since the terms on the right-hand side lie in $A^{k+l}$, this shows that $X_m=0$
  whenever $k +1 \le m \le k + l -1$. In particular, this shows that
  $\psi(\#{\mathfrak a}_k) \subset A^{k+l}$. Since $k <0$ here is arbitrary, we have
  proven that $\psi $ is homogeneous of degree $l$. But now we may rewrite \eqref{ruby6}
  as
  \begin{equation*}
    \sum_{m \ge l} m X_{m+k} \equiv l\sum_{m\ge k}\tau(Z,X_m) + \sum_{m\ge k}\tau(\delta, X_m)\modulo A^l.
  \end{equation*}
  Since $l \ge l + k + 1$, because $k < 0$, we have $A^l \subset A^{l +k +1}$, and it
  follows that
  \begin{align*}
    \sum_{m \ge l} m X_{m+k} &\equiv l\sum_{m\ge k}\tau(Z,X_m) + \sum_{m\ge k}\tau(\delta, X_m)\modulo A^{l+k+1}\\
    \implies lX_{l+k} &\equiv l \tau(Z, X_k) \modulo A^{l+k+1}\\
    \implies \psi(\#X) &\equiv \tau(Z, X) \modulo A^{l+k+1}.
  \end{align*}
\end{proof}

\refreshpage
\section{Model curvature}\label{modelcurvature}
Model curvature, defined for parabolic geometries in \ref{normalization}, makes sense for
an arbitrary infinitesimal filtered Cartan geometry $(A, \nabla, \tau)$, so long as we
restrict to the transitive case. However, it now depends on both $\tau $ and the
compatible connection $\nabla$, which is not generally determined uniquely by $\tau $. The
main goal of this section is to understand how model curvature transforms under Lie
algebroid automorphisms (Proposition \ref{transform}) and $\psi$-deformations
(Proposition \ref{curv_deform}). We additionally define the ``oid'' analogue of tractor
bundles \cite{Bailey_etal_94}, \cite[\S1.5.7]{Cap_Slovak_09} to explain the relationship
between infinitesimal Cartan connections on Lie algebroids and the adjoint tractor
connections appearing in the principal bundle approach to parabolic geometries.

\subsection{Model curvature and consequences of its vanishing}\label{model_curvature}
Given a transitive global or infinitesimal filtered Cartan geometry with underlying Lie
algebroid $\# \colon A \rightarrow TM$, let $\tau $ denote the model data and $\nabla $
the compatible infinitesimal Cartan connection. With Theorem \ref{curvature} in mind, the
difference between between $\torsion \bar\nabla$ (a ``deformed bracket'') and $\tau $ (the
model bracket) is the {\df model curvature} of the geometry. Specifically, this is
the section $\kappa$ of $\wedge^2 T^*\!M \otimes A$ defined by
\begin{equation*}
  \kappa(\#X, \#Y) = \torsion \bar\nabla (X, Y) - \tau(X, Y); \qquad X, Y \in \Gamma(A),
\end{equation*}
which makes sense, on account of the strong compatibility property
\eqrefs{compat2}{strong} and equation \eqrefs{hsd}{zero} defining $\bar\nabla $.

\begin{proposition}
  The model curvature $\kappa $ determines the curvature of $\nabla $ according to
  \begin{equation*}
    \curvature \nabla (U, V)X = (\bar\nabla_X \kappa)(U, V).
  \end{equation*}
  In particular, if $\kappa =0$, then $\curvature \nabla =0$ and
  $\torsion \bar\nabla =\tau $. If the geometry is regular, then the model curvature is
  homogeneous of degree one, i.e., $\kappa(U, V) \in \Gamma(A^{j+k+1})$ for
  $U \in \Gamma(T^jM)$ and $V \in \Gamma(T^kM)$; it is otherwise homogeneous of degree
  zero.
\end{proposition}
\noindent The consequences of $\curvature \nabla =0$ have already been discussed in
\ref{curvature}. At the very least, according to Theorem \ref{curvature}, $A$ will locally
be a transitive action algebroid, with the acting Lie algebra isomorphic to the Lie
algebra model for $\tau $.

\begin{proof}
  For any Cartan connection $\nabla $ on a transitive Lie algebroid, one has the easily
  derived identity,
  \begin{equation}
    \label{solidarity}
    \curvature\nabla(\#X, \#Y)Z =  \bar\nabla_Z\torsion \bar\nabla (X, Y).
  \end{equation}
  See, for example, \cite[\S5.4]{Blaom_06}. From the definition of $\kappa $,
  \begin{equation}
    \label{poland}
    (\bar\nabla_Z\kappa)(\#X, \#Y) = (\bar\nabla_Z\torsion \bar\nabla)(X, Y) -
    (\bar\nabla_Z \tau)(X, Y).
  \end{equation}
  The stated identity follows from \eqref{solidarity}, \eqref{poland} and the
  $\bar\nabla $-invariance of $\tau $ (compatibility of $\tau$ and $\nabla$).

  By definition,
  \begin{equation}
    \label{pot}
    \kappa(\#X, \#Y) = \bar\nabla_XY - \bar\nabla_YX - ([X, Y] + \tau(X, Y))
  \end{equation}
  Suppose $X \in \Gamma(A^j)$ and $Y \in \Gamma(A^k)$ for some $j, k < 0$. As we argued in
  the proof of Proposition \ref{homogeneous}, the non-positivity of $j$ and $k$ means that
  $A^j \subset A^{j+k+1}$ and $A^k \subset A^{j+k+1}$. By $\bar\nabla $-invariance of the
  filtration of $A$, the first two terms on the right-hand side of \eqref{pot} lie in
  $\Gamma(A^{j+k+1})$. The last bracketed term lies in $\Gamma(A^{j+k})$, by Axiom F1 for
  Lie algebroid filtrations, and compatibility of $\tau $ with the filtration of $A$. In
  the regular case, this bracketed term lies in $A^{j+k+1}$, by the definition of
  regularity.

\end{proof}

\subsection{Model curvature under automorphisms}\label{transform}
Let $A$ be a transitive filtered Lie algebroid, $\tau $ model data compatible with the
filtration, and $\nabla$ a $\tau$-compatible Cartan connection.  Let
$f \colon M \rightarrow M'$ be a diffeomorphism and $q \colon A \rightarrow A'$ some
filtration-preserving Lie algebroid isomorphism, covering $f$, into some second filtered
Lie algebroid $A'$. Supposing $A^0$ is the anchor kernel of $A$, the push-forward
$q_*\tau$, defined by
$$(q_*\tau)(X, Y) = q \tau(q^{-1}X, q^{-1}Y),$$ will be model data on $A'$. The isomorphism
$Tf \colon TM \rightarrow TM'$ will be filtration-preserving. In particular, $\tau $ is
regular if and only if $q_*\tau$ is regular. According to our next results, under $q$,
model curvature transforms in a natural way.

\begin{proposition}
  The equation
  \begin{equation}
    \label{tarragon1}
    \bar\nabla'_XY = q_*\bar\nabla_{q^*X} (q^*Y); \qquad X, Y \in \Gamma(A'),
  \end{equation}
  implicitly defines a Cartan connection $\nabla' $ compatible with the push-forward
  $\tau'=q_*\tau $. Here $(q_*X)(m)=qX(f^{-1}(m))$ and $(q^*X)(m) = q^{-1}X(f(m))$, for
  $X \in \Gamma(A)$. If ${\mathcal G}$ a Lie groupoid integrating $A$, ${\mathcal G}'$ is
  a firmly filtered Lie groupoid integrating $A'$, $\nabla $ the infinitesimalization of a
  Cartan connection $D$ on ${\mathcal G} $, and
  $Q \colon {\mathcal G} \rightarrow {\mathcal G}' $ a Lie groupoid isomorphism with
  infinitesimalization $q$, then
  \begin{equation}
    \label{tarragon2}
    \bar D_g' = q \circ \bar D_{Q^{-1}(g)} \circ q^{-1}
  \end{equation}
  implicitly defines a Cartan connection $D'$ on ${\mathcal G}' $ compatible with
  $\tau' $, and infinitesimalizing to $\nabla'$. In any case, if $\kappa$ is the model
  curvature of $(\tau, \nabla)$ and $\kappa'$ the model curvature of $(\tau', \nabla')$,
  viewed as sections of $\wedge^2 T^*\!M \otimes {\mathcal A}$ and
  $\wedge^2 T^*\!M' \otimes {\mathcal A}'$, then we obtain the {\df transformation rule},
  \begin{equation}
    \label{tarragon5}
    \kappa'(V_1, V_2) = q \kappa (Tf^{-1} \cdot V_1, Tf^{-1}\cdot V_2); \qquad V_1, V_2 \in TM.
  \end{equation}
  If $({\mathcal G}, \tau, D)$ (resp., $(A, \tau, \nabla)$) is an (infinitesimal) filtered
  Cartan geometry, then $({\mathcal G}, \tau', D')$ (resp., $(A, \tau', \nabla')$) is an
  (infinitesimal) filtered Cartan geometry. In the special case that $Q$ (resp., $q$) is
  an (infinitesimal) Weyl gauge transformation (where $A=A'$ and $f = \identity$) the
  associated (infinitesimal) Levi structures for the primed and unprimed geometries are
  identical.
\end{proposition}
\begin{proof}
  To show $\nabla'$ is well-defined, we need to apply
  Proposition \ref{hsd}, which means showing: (i) $\bar\nabla'$, as defined by
  \eqref{tarragon1}, is a representation, and supposing $\#Y=0$, that (ii)
  $\bar\nabla'_XY = [X, Y]$. Verifying (i) is is an easy computation appealing to the fact
  that $\bar\nabla $ is a representation and that $q$ is a Lie algebroid
  morphism. Regarding (ii), we have
  \begin{equation*}
    \bar\nabla'_XY = q_*\bar\nabla_{q^*X}(q^*Y) = q_*[q^*X, q^*Y] = [X, Y],
  \end{equation*}
  where the second equality follows from the fact that
  $\bar\nabla_{\xi}{\eta} = [\xi, \eta]$ whenever $\# \eta =0$, and that
  $\# (q^*Y) = f^*(\# Y)$ for any $Y \in \Gamma(A)$. Since $\tau $ is $\bar\nabla$-invariant
  by hypothesis, another easy computation shows that $\tau'$ is $\bar\nabla'$-invariant,
  i.e., is compatible with $\bar\nabla'$.

  Regarding the global case, we prove a little more, indicating the origins of formulas
  \eqref{tarragon1} and \eqref{tarragon2}. Note first that because $Q$ is a groupoid
  morphism, we have the identity
  \begin{equation}
    \label{tarragon3}
    q \circ \Adjoint_\mu = \Adjoint_{(J^1Q)\mu} \circ q; \qquad \mu \in J^1 {\mathcal G},
  \end{equation}
  where $\Adjoint$ is the adjoint representation of $J^1 {\mathcal G} $ on $A $
  (see \cite{Blaom_16b}). For a proof of \eqref{tarragon3}, suppose $\mu = J^1_mb$, for
  some bisection $b$ of $\mathcal G$. Then for an arbitrary element of $A$, represented by
  source-fibre path $t \mapsto g(t)$ beginning at $m$, we have
  \begin{equation*}
    \Adjoint_{J^1_m b}\left(\frac{d}{dt}g(t)\Big|_{t=0}\right)
    = \frac{d}{dt}b(g(t)m)g(t)b(m)^{-1}\Big|_{t=0},
  \end{equation*}
  so that
  \begin{multline*}
    (q \circ \Adjoint_{J^1_m b})\left(\frac{d}{dt}g(t)\Big|_{t=0}\right)
    = \frac{d}{dt}Q(b(g(t)m))Q(g(t))Q(b(m))^{-1}\Big|_{t=0}\\
    = \Adjoint_{(J^1Q)(J^1_m b)}  \frac{d}{dt}Q(g(t))\Big|_{t=0}
    = \Adjoint_{(J^1Q)(J^1_m b)}  q\left(\frac{d}{dt}g(t)\Big|_{t=0}\right).
  \end{multline*}
  and \eqref{tarragon3} is proven. If
  $S \colon {\mathcal G} \rightarrow J^1 {\mathcal G} $ is the splitting associated with
  $D$, then associated with the splitting
  \begin{equation}
    \label{tarragon4}
      S ' = J^1 Q \circ S \circ Q^{-1}
  \end{equation}
  is a Cartan connection $D'$ on ${\mathcal G}'$, and applying the identity
  \eqref{tarragon3} and the definition of representations $\bar D $ and $\bar D'$
  associated with these connections, we obtain the formula \eqref{tarragon2}. Showing that
  $\bar\nabla'$ is the infinitesimalization of $\bar D'$ is a simple computation. The
  $\bar D'$-invariance of $\tau'$ readily follows from the $\bar D$-invariance of $\tau $,
  i.e., $\tau' $ is indeed compatible with $D'$.

  Regarding \eqref{tarragon5}, we compute, for any $X, Y \in \Gamma(A)$,
  \begin{align*}
    \kappa'(\#X, \#Y) &= \bar\nabla'_XY - \bar\nabla'_YX - [X, Y] - \tau'(X, Y)\\
                      &= q_*\bar\nabla_{q^*X}(q^*Y) - q_*\bar\nabla_{q^*Y}(q^*X)
                        - q_*[q^*X, q^*Y] - q_*\left(\,\tau(q^*X, q^*Y)\,\right) \\
    &= q_*\left(\,\kappa(\# q^*X, \# q^*Y)\,\right) = q_*\left(\,\kappa(f^*(\# X), f^*\# Y)\,\right),
  \end{align*}
  and \eqref{tarragon5} follows.

  The proof of statements regarding the special case of Weyl gauge transformations are not
  difficult, after one applies Lemma \ref{deformations} to see that
  $\graded_0(\tau)=\graded_0(\tau')$ in that case. Details are left to the reader.
\end{proof}

\subsection{The Kostant codifferential}\label{homology}
Let $A$ be a filtered Lie algebroid with filtration-compatible model data $\tau $. For the
moment, the Lie algebra model for $\tau $ is arbitrary; it need not be reductive, and we
need not suppose $A$ is transitive. However we will assume $A$ admits a $\tau$-compatible
Weyl gauge.

Recall from \ref{normalization} that we have a natural chain complex

\begin{equation}
  \label{chain1} 0 \leftpartial{\tau} A \leftpartial{\tau} A^1 \otimes A
\leftpartial{\tau} \wedge^2 A^1 \otimes A \leftpartial{\tau} \cdots,
\end{equation}
where the Kostant codifferential $\partial^\tau$ is defined by
\eqrefs{normalization}{form1}. In the proposition below, we will establish that the
corresponding bundles of homology groups have realizations depending only on
$T = \graded_0(\tau)$, and are canonically {\em graded}, and not just canonically
filtered.

Notice that the bracket $T = \graded_0(\tau)$ makes $\graded(A)$ into a representation of
the Lie algebra bundle $\graded(A^1)$ and we obtain a graded version of \eqref{chain1},
\begin{equation}
  \label{chain2} 0 \leftpartial{*}  \graded(A)
  \leftpartial{*} \graded(A^1) \otimes \graded(A)
  \leftpartial{*} \wedge^2 \graded(A^1) \otimes \graded(A) \leftpartial{*} \cdots,
\end{equation}
where $\partial^*$ is defined by the same formula \eqrefs{normalization}{form1}, with $\tau $ there
replaced with $T$.

The filtration of $A$ induces a filtration of each term in the complex \eqref{chain1}; for
example decomposable elements of $(\wedge^2 A^1 \otimes A)^l$ are of the form
$Y\wedge Z \otimes X$, for some $Y\in A^i$, $Z \in A^j$ and $X \in A^k$ with $i, j \ge 1$
and $i + j +k = l$. Similarly, each term of the complex \eqref{chain2} is graded. The
differential $\partial^\tau$ is filtration-preserving, while $\partial^*$ is
grading-preserving. There is no canonical chain map from complex \eqref{chain1} to
\eqref{chain2}. However, for each fixed $l \in {\mathbb Z} $, we have subcomplexes
\begin{gather}
  \label{chain3} 0 \leftpartial{\tau}  A^l \leftpartial{\tau} (A^1\otimes A)^l \leftpartial{\tau} (\wedge^2 A^1 \otimes A)^l \leftpartial{\tau} \cdots \\
  \label{chain4} 0 \leftpartial{*}  \graded(A)_l
  \leftpartial{*} (\graded(A^1) \otimes \graded(A))_l
  \leftpartial{*} (\wedge^2 \graded(A^1) \otimes \graded(A))_l \leftpartial{*} \cdots,
\end{gather}
and $\graded$ is a chain map from \eqref{chain3} to \eqref{chain4}.

We let $H_n(A^1, A)$, $H_n(\graded(A^1), \graded(A))$, $H_n(A^1, A)^l$, and
$H_n(\graded(A^1),\graded(A))_l$ denote the degree $n$ homologies of the complexes
\eqref{chain1}, \eqref{chain2}, \eqref{chain3}, and \eqref{chain4}, understood as vector
bundles over $M$. Because $\partial^\tau $ is filtration-preserving and $\partial^*$ is
grading-preserving, for each $l \in {\mathbb Z}$, the natural morphisms
\begin{align*}
  H_n(A^1,A)^l &\rightarrow H_n(A^1,A)\\
  H_n(\graded(A^1),\graded(A))_l &\rightarrow H_n(\graded(A^1),\graded(A))
\end{align*}
are injective, and we see easily that this allows us to view $H_n(A^1, A)$ as a filtered
vector bundle, and $H_n(\graded(A^1),\graded(A))$ as a graded vector bundle.

Each term in the complex \eqref{chain1} is a representation of $A^1$, and $\partial^\tau $
is equivariant with respect to these representations, so that $H_n(A^1, A)$ is a also an
$A^1$-representation.  These integrate to representations of the bundle of
simply-connected nilpotent Lie groups $\exp(A^1)$ integrating $A^1$.  In the case $A$ is
integrated by some Lie groupoid ${\mathcal G} $ admitting a Weyl gauge, we may identify
$\exp(A^1)$ with a normal subgroupoid ${\mathcal G}^1 \subset {\mathcal G} $, by
Proposition \ref{weyl2}.

\begin{proposition}
  Let $A$ be a filtered Lie algebroid and $\tau $ model data compatible with the
  filtration. Then:
  \begin{conditions}
  \item The actions of $A^1 $ and $\exp(A^1)$ on $H_n(A^1, A)$ are trivial. In particular,
    if $\nabla $ is a Cartan connection on $A$ compatible with $\tau $, then the
    representation $\bar\nabla $ of $A$ on itself makes $H_n(A^1,A)$ into an
    $A/A^1$-representation. In the global case, if $D$ is a $\tau$-compatible Cartan
    connection on ${\mathcal G} $, then the representation $\bar D $ of ${\mathcal G} $ on
    $A$ makes $H_n(A^1,A)$ into ${\mathcal G}/{\mathcal G}^1$-representation. \label{hay1}
  \item For each Weyl gauge $\epsilon$ compatible with $\tau $, the canonical isomorphism
    associated with the splitting $\Phi_\epsilon \colon \graded(A) \rightarrow A$,
    $$\tilde \Phi_\epsilon \colon \wedge^n \graded(A^1) \otimes \graded(A) \rightarrow \wedge^n A^1 \otimes A$$
    is a chain map between the complexes \eqref{chain2} and \eqref{chain1}.
    \label{hay2}
  \item The corresponding isomorphism in homology
    $$ (\tilde \Phi_\epsilon)_* \colon H_n(\graded(A^1), \graded(A)) \rightarrow H_n(A^1, A)$$
    is independent of the choice of $\epsilon$. In particular, if $A$ admits a Weyl gauge, then
    the filtered vector bundle $H_n(A^1, A)$ has a canonical splitting. \label{hay3}
  \end{conditions}
\end{proposition}

\begin{lemma}
  Let $\Adjoint^\tau $ denote the representation of of $\exp(A^1)$ on $A$ and let
  $\epsilon_1, \epsilon_2$ be two Weyl gauges compatible with $\tau $. Then there exists a smooth
  section $k$ of $\exp(A^1)$ such that
  $\Phi_{\epsilon_2}(\xi) = \Adjoint^\tau_{k(m)}\Phi_{\epsilon_1}(\xi)$, for any
  $\xi \in \graded(A)|_{m}$.
\end{lemma}
\begin{proof}
  Applying Lemma \eqrefs{splittings}{splittings1} fibre-wise, there is a unique section
  $k $ of the bundle of simply-connected nilpotent Lie groups $\exp(A^1)$ such that
  $\epsilon_2(m) = \Adjoint^\tau_{k(m)} \epsilon_1(m)$. Since we suppose $\epsilon_1$ and
  $\epsilon_2$ are smooth, $k$ must be also. The desired result now follows from the
  fibre-wise application of \eqrefs{splittings}{splittings2}.
\end{proof}

\begin{proof}[Proof of proposition]
  In proving \eqref{hay1}, it suffices to prove the claim for $A^1$, since $\exp(A^1)$ has
  connected source-fibres. We need to show that $A^1$ maps the kernel of
  $\partial^\tau \colon \wedge^n A^1 \otimes A \rightarrow \wedge^{n-1}A^1 \otimes A$ into
  the image of
  $\partial^\tau \colon \wedge^{n+1}A^1 \otimes A \rightarrow \wedge^n A^1 \otimes
  A$. Following \cite[p.~263]{Cap_Slovak_09}, we see this follows from the identity
  \begin{equation*}
    -\adjoint_Y^\tau \omega =
    \partial^\tau(Y \wedge \omega) +
    Y \wedge \partial^\tau \omega;
    \qquad \omega \in \Gamma(\wedge^n A^1 \otimes A),\,Y \in \Gamma(A^1).
  \end{equation*}
  To prove the identity, it suffices to prove it for decomposable $\omega $. For example,
  if $\omega = Z \otimes X$ ($n = 1$), then we compute
  \begin{align*}
    \partial^\tau(Y \wedge \omega) &= - Z \otimes \tau(Y, X) + Y \otimes \tau(Z, X) - \tau(Y,Z) \otimes X\\
    Y \wedge \partial^\tau \omega &= Y \wedge (-\tau(Z, X)),\\
    \text{so that}\quad \partial^\tau (Y \wedge \omega) + Y \wedge \partial^\tau \omega &=
    -Z \otimes \tau(Y,X) - \tau(Y,Z) \otimes X = - \adjoint^\tau_Y \omega.
  \end{align*}
  See op.~cited for the general argument.

  The definition of $\tilde \Phi_\epsilon$ is clear. For example, we have
  $\tilde \Phi_\epsilon(Z_1 \wedge Z_2 \otimes X) = \Phi_\epsilon(Z_1)\wedge
  \Phi_\epsilon(Z_2) \wedge \Phi_\epsilon(X)$. To prove \eqref{hay2}, it suffices to show
  that
  $\partial^\tau\tilde \Phi_\epsilon \omega = \tilde \Phi_\epsilon \partial^* \omega $ for
  all $\omega \in \wedge^{n+1} \graded(A^1) \otimes \graded(A)$ that is decomposable,
  which is readily accomplished: Take $\omega$ to be of the form
  $\graded(Y_0) \wedge \ldots \wedge \graded(Y_n) \otimes \graded(X)$, where, without loss
  of generality, we suppose $Y_0,\ldots,Y_n$ and $X$ each lie in some component
  ${\mathfrak a}_j$, in the decomposition $A=\oplus_i {\mathfrak a}_i$ associated with
  $\epsilon $ ($j\ge 1$ in the case of $Y_0,\ldots,Y_n$). Part \eqref{hay3} now follows
  from preceding parts and the lemma above.
